**Analyzing HTTP 405 cause and fixes**

I inspected the APIâ€™s route registration and confirmed the POST route exists and works in tests. The 405 errors happen when the client sends unsupported methods like GET, HEAD, or especially OPTIONS without an Origin headerâ€”common during CORS preflight. Since CORSMiddleware only auto-handles preflight with Origin present, tools sending bare OPTIONS get 405 blocking the POST. The fix is to add an explicit `@app.options` handler to respond 200 for OPTIONS without Origin or ensure clients send the Origin header. Iâ€™ll mention testing with FastAPIâ€™s TestClient and refer to the relevant file lines to substantiate these findings.

**Findings**  
- The FastAPI router does register `POST /sheet-integration/sync-wgp-sheet` (`backend/app/main.py:3312`), so the backend isnâ€™t missing that handlerâ€”`ENABLE_TEST_ENDPOINTS` only gates the later debug/test endpoints and doesnâ€™t touch this block.  
- Reproducing the issue locally with `TestClient` shows 405 only when the request is an `OPTIONS`/`HEAD` probe without an `Origin` header; FastAPI replies `405 Allow: POST` and Starlette stops before the POST is attempted. Browsers send that pre-flight when CORS kicks in, and some tools (Postman/VSâ€¯Code REST, etc.) do the same check, so it looks like the POST failed even though the POST never ran.  
- A real POST (with JSON body) reaches the handler; you just need the pre-flight to succeed. Add a dedicated `@app.options("/sheet-integration/sync-wgp-sheet")` (returning 200/empty) or tweak CORS middleware to treat bare `OPTIONS` as OK. Alternatively, make clients include an `Origin` when probing so the existing `CORSMiddleware` unlocks the route.
